## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow Security Audit

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes)
**Task Type:** Security Analysis (analysis only — no code changes)

## Scenario

You are a security engineer auditing the Kubernetes API server's RBAC authorization subsystem. Your goal is to trace the complete authorization flow from when an API request arrives to when a permission decision (allow/deny) is made, mapping the attack surface and identifying security controls.

## Your Task

Analyze the Kubernetes RBAC authorization flow and write a comprehensive security analysis. Trace how API requests are authorized, identify entry points where untrusted input enters the authorization decision path, map the data flow through authorization plugins, and assess the security posture of the RBAC implementation.

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

## Required Sections

### Files Examined
- List each file you analyzed and its role in the RBAC authorization flow

### Entry Points
1. Identify where API requests enter the authorization subsystem
2. Identify where RBAC policy data (roles, bindings) enters the system
3. Note any places where untrusted input could influence authorization decisions

### Data Flow
Trace the authorization flow through these stages:
1. **Request arrival** — HTTP handler receives the request
2. **Authentication** — Request identity is established
3. **Authorization filter** — Request is routed to authorizer chain
4. **RBAC evaluation** — Role and binding resolution, permission check
5. **Decision** — Allow/deny outcome and audit logging

For each stage, name the specific file, function, and data structures involved.

### Dependency Chain
Provide an ordered list of files from request entry to authorization decision.

### Analysis
- What vulnerability classes could apply (auth bypass, privilege escalation, policy misconfiguration)?
- What existing mitigations are in place?
- What are the security boundaries between authorization plugins?
- How does the authorizer chain (RBAC, Node, Webhook) interact?

### Summary
Concise description of the RBAC authorization security posture and key findings.

## Constraints

- **Analysis only** — do NOT modify any source files
- Be specific — include file paths, function names, and type names
- Focus on the `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/` and `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/` directories

If the decision is `DecisionAllow` the request is passed to the next handler; otherwise `403 Forbidden` is returned.\n\n**Untrusted input that enters the authorization decision path:**\n\n| Source | Field | Used in |\n|--------|-------|---------|\n| HTTP method | `Verb` | `AttributesRecord.Verb` \u2192 all rule match calls |\n| URL path | parsed by `RequestInfo` | `Resource`, `Subresource`, `Namespace`, `Name`, `APIGroup`, `APIVersion`, `Path` |\n| HTTP headers `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Extra-*`, `Impersonate-Uid` | subject identity | `WithImpersonation` builds `actingAsAttributes`; if all authorized, replaces `user.Info` |\n| Query parameter `fieldSelector` | `FieldSelectorRequirements` | used when feature gate `AuthorizeWithSelectors` is enabled |\n| Query parameter `labelSelector` | `LabelSelectorRequirements` | same |\n| TLS client certificate / bearer token / OIDC token | authenticated `user.Info` | `GetUser()` in every rule check |\n\n### 2. Where RBAC policy data enters the system\n\nPolicy data flows in through the `SharedInformerFactory` cache backed by the Kubernetes etcd store:\n\n- **Roles** \u2014 `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().Roles().Lister()` \u2192 `RoleGetter.GetRole()`\n- **RoleBindings** \u2014 `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().RoleBindings().Lister()` \u2192 `RoleBindingLister.ListRoleBindings()`\n- **ClusterRoles** \u2014 `.ClusterRoles().Lister()` \u2192 `ClusterRoleGetter.GetClusterRole()`\n- **ClusterRoleBindings** \u2014 `.ClusterRoleBindings().Lister()` \u2192 `ClusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings()`\n\nThese listers read from the in-memory informer cache, which is periodically synced from etcd; they **do not** make live API calls on the authorization hot path.\n\n### 3. Untrusted input that can influence authorization decisions\n\n1. **User-controlled HTTP headers** \u2014 `Impersonate-*` headers, if the caller has `impersonate` RBAC permission, allow full identity substitution including arbitrary extra claims.\n2. **Field/label selectors** \u2014 When `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate is enabled, these query parameters are parsed and forwarded as part of `AttributesRecord`. A webhook authorizer can use them; the built-in RBAC evaluator does not match on selector requirements.\n3. **RBAC objects in etcd** \u2014 Any principal that can write `Role`, `ClusterRole`, `RoleBinding`, or `ClusterRoleBinding` objects can escalate permissions, subject to the `ConfirmNoEscalation` guard.\n4. **Webhook authorization configuration** \u2014 The `--authorization-config` file (or live-reload file) controls which external webhook endpoints receive `SubjectAccessReview` requests.\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Stage 1 \u2014 Request Arrival\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`  \n**Function:** `withAuthentication()` (line 50)  \n**Data structures:** `http.Request`, `authenticator.Response`, `user.Info`\n\nThe Go `net/http` server receives a TLS connection. The `withAuthentication` HTTP handler calls `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)`, which invokes the authenticator chain (x509 client cert, bearer token, OIDC, bootstrap token, etc.). On success it stores `resp.User` (a `user.Info` \u2014 name, UID, groups, extra) into the request context. On failure, `failed.ServeHTTP()` returns `401 Unauthorized`. The `Authorization` header and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers are deleted from the request to prevent downstream misuse.\n\n### Stage 2 \u2014 Authentication\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`  \n**Function:** `withAuthentication()` \u2192 `genericapirequest.WithUser(req.Context(), resp.User)`\n\nThe authenticated `user.Info` is placed on the Go `context.Context` and propagated through the handler chain. All subsequent authorization checks pull the identity from the context via `request.UserFrom(ctx)`. If no authenticator matches, the user is set to `system:anonymous` with group `system:unauthenticated`.\n\n### Stage 3 \u2014 Authorization Filter\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`  \n**Functions:** `WithAuthorization()` (line 53), `withAuthorization()` (line 57), `GetAuthorizerAttributes()` (line 100)\n\n`GetAuthorizerAttributes()` constructs an `authorizer.AttributesRecord` by reading:\n- `user.Info` from context (set during authentication / impersonation)\n- `RequestInfo` from context (parsed URL: verb, resource, subresource, namespace, name, API group, API version, path)\n- Optionally: field/label selectors if feature gate `AuthorizeWithSelectors` is enabled\n\nThe `AttributesRecord` is passed to `a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)` where `a` is the composite `unionAuthzHandler`. The result is:\n- `DecisionAllow` \u2192 audit annotation `authorization.k8s.io/decision=allow`, pass to handler\n- `DecisionNoOpinion` with no error \u2192 `403 Forbidden` + audit annotation `authorization.k8s.io/decision=forbid`\n- Error \u2192 audit annotation `authorization.k8s.io/reason=internal error`, `500 Internal Server Error`\n\n**Important note (line 78\u201385):** The check `authorized == authorizer.DecisionAllow` is evaluated *before* checking `err != nil`. This means an RBAC authorizer that encounters evaluation errors but still finds a matching allow rule will grant access \u2014 errors are non-fatal per the RBAC design contract.\n\n### Stage 4 \u2014 RBAC Evaluation\n\n**Files and functions in evaluation order:**\n\n1. **`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go`** \u2014 `reloadableAuthorizerResolver.newForConfig()` (line 87)  \n   Builds the authorizer list. The first entry is always `privilegedGroupAuthorizer{groups: [\"system:masters\"]}`, which short-circuits to `DecisionAllow` for any member of `system:masters` regardless of RBAC rules.\n\n2. **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`** \u2014 `unionAuthzHandler.Authorize()` (line 45)  \n   Iterates through the ordered chain (`system:masters` fast-path \u2192 Node \u2192 RBAC \u2192 Webhook, in configured order). Returns the first `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`. `DecisionNoOpinion` causes iteration to the next authorizer.\n\n3. **`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`** \u2014 `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize()` (line 75)  \n   Creates an `authorizingVisitor` and calls `r.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(ctx, requestAttributes.GetUser(), requestAttributes.GetNamespace(), visitor.visit)`.\n\n4. **`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`** \u2014 `DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor()` (line 179)  \n   **Phase A \u2014 ClusterRoleBindings:** Lists all `ClusterRoleBinding` objects. For each, calls `appliesTo(user, binding.Subjects, \"\")` to check if the requesting user matches any subject (by exact name for `User`, group membership for `Group`, or `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername()` for `ServiceAccount`). On a match, fetches the referenced `ClusterRole` or `Role` via `GetRoleReferenceRules()` and invokes the visitor with each `PolicyRule`.  \n   **Phase B \u2014 RoleBindings (namespace-scoped):** If the request has a non-empty namespace, repeats the same process for `RoleBinding` objects in that namespace.\n\n5. **`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`** \u2014 `DefaultRuleResolver.GetRoleReferenceRules()` (line 240)  \n   Resolves the role reference: if `roleRef.Kind == \"Role\"`, calls `roleGetter.GetRole(ctx, namespace, name)`; if `\"ClusterRole\"`, calls `clusterRoleGetter.GetClusterRole(ctx, name)`. Returns `role.Rules` or an error. An unresolvable `roleRef.Kind` returns an error that is collected but does not stop evaluation of other bindings.\n\n6. **`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`** \u2014 `authorizingVisitor.visit()` (line 63) \u2192 `RuleAllows()` (line 178)  \n   For each `PolicyRule`, calls:\n   - `rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches(rule, verb)` \u2014 exact match or `\"*\"` wildcard\n   - `rbacv1helpers.APIGroupMatches(rule, apiGroup)` \u2014 exact match or `\"*\"` wildcard\n   - `rbacv1helpers.ResourceMatches(rule, combinedResource, subresource)` \u2014 exact match on `resource/subresource`, `\"*\"`, or `*/subresource` pattern\n   - `rbacv1helpers.ResourceNameMatches(rule, name)` \u2014 exact name match; empty `ResourceNames` matches all names\n\n   All four must be true simultaneously. For non-resource requests, only `VerbMatches` + `NonResourceURLMatches` (which supports suffix `*` wildcards) are evaluated.\n\n7. **`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`** \u2014 `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize()` returns `DecisionAllow` if any rule matches, or `DecisionNoOpinion` if none do (RBAC never explicitly denies).\n\n### Stage 5 \u2014 Decision and Audit Logging\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`  \n**Functions:** `withAuthorization()` (line 57), `audit.AddAuditAnnotations()` (line 80/93)\n\nAfter `a.Authorize()` returns:\n\n- **Allow:** `audit.AddAuditAnnotations(ctx, \"authorization.k8s.io/decision\", \"allow\", \"authorization.k8s.io/reason\", reason)` is set, then the downstream handler is invoked. The `reason` string is `\"RBAC: allowed by <binding description>\"` and is included in the audit event.\n- **Deny:** `audit.AddAuditAnnotations(ctx, \"authorization.k8s.io/decision\", \"forbid\", \"authorization.k8s.io/reason\", reason)` is set and `responsewriters.Forbidden()` returns `403`.\n- **Error:** `audit.AddAuditAnnotation(ctx, \"authorization.k8s.io/reason\", \"internal error\")` is set and `500 Internal Server Error` is returned.\n\nMetrics are recorded by `authorizationmetrics.InstrumentedAuthorizer` wrapping each plugin (set up in `reload.go`). Latency, decision outcome, and authorizer type are all tracked as Prometheus metrics.\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered list from HTTP request entry to final authorization decision:\n\n```\n1.  net/http server (TLS accept)\n2.  staging/.../filters/authentication.go       WithAuthentication()\n      \u2192 auth.AuthenticateRequest()\n      \u2192 genericapirequest.WithUser(ctx, user.Info)\n3.  staging/.../filters/impersonation.go        WithImpersonation()\n      \u2192 buildImpersonationRequests(req.Header)\n      \u2192 a.Authorize() [impersonate verb check per target]\n      \u2192 request.WithUser(ctx, newUser)\n4.  staging/.../filters/authorization.go        WithAuthorization()\n      \u2192 GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx) \u2192 authorizer.AttributesRecord\n      \u2192 a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n5.  pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go      reloadableAuthorizerResolver.Authorize()\n      \u2192 r.current.Load().authorizer.Authorize()\n6.  staging/.../authorization/union/union.go    unionAuthzHandler.Authorize()\n      \u2192 privilegedGroupAuthorizer.Authorize()   [system:masters fast-path]\n      \u2192 (Node authorizer, if configured)\n      \u2192 RBACAuthorizer.Authorize()              [if RBAC in chain]\n      \u2192 (Webhook authorizer, if configured)\n7.  plugin/.../rbac/rbac.go                     RBACAuthorizer.Authorize()\n      \u2192 DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor()\n8.  pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go        DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor()\n      \u2192 ClusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings()\n      \u2192 appliesTo(user, subjects, namespace)\n      \u2192 DefaultRuleResolver.GetRoleReferenceRules() \u2192 ClusterRoleGetter / RoleGetter\n      \u2192 visitor.visit(source, &rule, err)\n      \u2192 (repeat for RoleBindingLister.ListRoleBindings() if namespaced)\n9.  plugin/.../rbac/rbac.go                     authorizingVisitor.visit() \u2192 RuleAllows()\n10. pkg/apis/rbac/v1/evaluation_helpers.go      VerbMatches / APIGroupMatches /\n                                                ResourceMatches / ResourceNameMatches /\n                                                NonResourceURLMatches\n11. staging/.../filters/authorization.go        audit.AddAuditAnnotations() + response\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Vulnerability Classes\n\n#### 1. Privilege Escalation via RBAC Object Manipulation\n\n**Class:** Privilege escalation through policy misconfiguration.\n\nAny principal that can `create`, `update`, or `patch` `ClusterRole`, `ClusterRoleBinding`, `Role`, or `RoleBinding` objects can escalate their own permissions, **subject to the escalation guard in `ConfirmNoEscalation()`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:53`). This guard checks that the user's current rules fully *cover* the rules in the object they are trying to grant. However:\n\n- If the rule-resolver returns an incomplete rule set (due to intermittent errors), `ConfirmNoEscalation` may proceed with a reduced rule set and potentially allow a grant that should be blocked. The code explicitly notes this is non-fatal (line 63\u201367).\n- If a user already has `escalate` or `bind` verbs on a role, they bypass `ConfirmNoEscalation` entirely (this is by design but must be tightly controlled).\n- Operators that grant `*` on `rbac.authorization.k8s.io` effectively gain cluster admin.\n\n#### 2. Impersonation-Based Identity Spoofing\n\n**Class:** Authentication bypass / privilege escalation through impersonation.\n\n`WithImpersonation` (`filters/impersonation.go`) parses `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Extra-*`, and `Impersonate-Uid` headers. Each impersonation target requires an explicit RBAC authorization check with verb `\"impersonate\"` against the requesting user's identity. However:\n\n- `UserExtra` key names are parsed from the header key by converting them to lowercase and URL-unescaping (`unescapeExtraKey`, line 241). A malformed or percent-encoded key is always accepted (fallback to raw value), meaning extra keys are stored even if they cannot be cleanly parsed. Downstream code relying on exact extra key matching could mismatch.\n- If impersonation of `system:anonymous` is allowed, the impersonated user gets group `system:unauthenticated` (line 154), but retains the same permissions as any other allowed impersonation target. An operator granting `impersonate` for `system:anonymous` is effectively opening a path to anonymous access from an authenticated principal.\n- `system:masters` membership in the *impersonated* identity would grant full cluster access through `privilegedGroupAuthorizer`. Impersonation of groups requires `impersonate` on `groups`, but there is no additional guard preventing impersonation of `system:masters` specifically if the RBAC rules allow it.\n\n#### 3. `DecisionNoOpinion` Fallthrough / Auth Bypass if Chain is Empty\n\n**Class:** Authorization bypass.\n\n- If the `AuthorizationConfiguration` is missing a required authorizer and somehow the chain is constructed with only the superuser fast-path, any authenticated user (not in `system:masters`) would receive `DecisionNoOpinion` from the union, which maps to `403`. This is safe by default.\n- However, if `AlwaysAllow` is included anywhere in the chain (e.g., for testing as seen in `hack/make-rules/test-cmd.sh`), it short-circuits after RBAC with a blanket allow. The code does warn (`klog.Warning(\"Authorization is disabled\")`) only when the `Authorizer` is nil.\n- The `path.NewAuthorizer` allow-list for non-resource paths (`/healthz`, `/metrics`, etc.) is additive: it returns `DecisionNoOpinion` for resource requests but `DecisionAllow` for matching non-resource paths. Misconfiguration of the allow-list can expose health/metrics endpoints unauthenticated if placed before the RBAC authorizer in the chain.\n\n#### 4. Webhook Failure Policy \u2014 Fail-Open Risk\n\n**Class:** Authorization bypass under degraded conditions.\n\nWhen a Webhook authorizer is configured with `failurePolicy: NoOpinion` (`authzconfig.FailurePolicyNoOpinion`), a webhook that is unreachable or returns an error causes the authorizer to return `DecisionNoOpinion`, which falls through to the next authorizer or eventually results in a deny. This is the safer default.\n\nHowever, if `failurePolicy: Deny` is used and the webhook fails, `DecisionDeny` is returned, causing all requests to fail if the webhook is the primary authorizer. Operators typically choose `NoOpinion` for availability, making the chain effectively RBAC-only if the webhook is down \u2014 which may be intentional but is a security boundary that must be documented.\n\nWebhook responses are cached (configurable TTL for allow and deny) in an in-memory cache. A compromised or misconfigured cache TTL could cause stale allow decisions to persist.\n\n#### 5. RBAC Returns `DecisionNoOpinion` for Denials (No Explicit Deny)\n\n**Class:** Policy misconfiguration risk.\n\nA critical design property: `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize()` **never** returns `DecisionDeny`. On a rule miss it returns `DecisionNoOpinion` (line 126). This means RBAC cannot explicitly forbid an action \u2014 it can only fail to allow it, relying on the union chain to ultimately deny by exhaustion. If a later authorizer in the chain (e.g., `AlwaysAllow`) is present, RBAC's \"no match\" is irrelevant. Operators must ensure no permissive authorizer follows RBAC in the chain.\n\n#### 6. `system:masters` Permanent Superuser Bypass\n\n**Class:** Access control bypass (by design but a security boundary).\n\n`privilegedGroupAuthorizer` is *always* inserted as the **first** authorizer in `newForConfig()` (line 98\u201399), before any configured authorizer. Any principal with `system:masters` in their groups bypasses RBAC entirely. This group is typically used for the API server's own loopback client and kubeadm bootstrap but cannot be removed or audited via RBAC \u2014 there are no RBAC rules referencing it. The only way to track its use is via audit logs.\n\n---\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n| Mitigation | Location | Effect |\n|------------|----------|--------|\n| Header stripping post-authentication | `filters/authentication.go:88\u2013107` | Prevents injection of `Authorization`, `X-Remote-*` proxy headers after authentication succeeds |\n| Per-target impersonation authorization | `filters/impersonation.go:117` | Each impersonated entity requires its own `impersonate` RBAC check |\n| `ConfirmNoEscalation` privilege escalation guard | `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:53` | Prevents granting permissions beyond what the grantor holds |\n| `DecisionNoOpinion` default denial | `plugin/.../rbac/rbac.go:126` | RBAC never allows by default; deny is the baseline |\n| Audit annotations on every authorization decision | `filters/authorization.go:80\u201395` | Every allow/deny is recorded with reason, enabling forensic analysis |\n| Authorizer metrics instrumentation | `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go:108,164` | Prometheus metrics track per-authorizer latency and decisions |\n| `system:masters` superuser only accessible via in-cluster trust | `authorizerfactory/builtin.go:72\u201395` | Cannot be granted via RBAC; only set through authentication (cert SANs) |\n| Informer cache for policy lookups | `rbac.RoleGetter` / `RoleBindingLister` | Policy data is read from in-memory cache, not directly from etcd on each request \u2014 prevents etcd DOS |\n| Hot-reload validation with `requireNonWebhookTypes` | `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go:204` | Prevents removing non-webhook authorizer types from the chain at runtime |\n| Webhook retry backoff | `authorizerfactory/delegating.go:48` | Limits fan-out storms when webhook is degraded |\n\n---\n\n### Security Boundaries Between Authorization Plugins\n\nThe union chain (`union.go`) provides **first-match-wins** semantics for `Allow` and `Deny`. This creates clear but sharp security boundaries:\n\n1. **`system:masters` fast-path** is always first and cannot be overridden by any downstream authorizer.\n2. **Node authorizer** runs before RBAC in the typical `Node,RBAC` configuration. It enforces node-specific rules using a graph model (nodes, pods, PVs, volume attachments). Its rules are independent of RBAC and cannot be extended by RBAC policies. A node is not allowed to read secrets outside its assigned pods regardless of RBAC.\n3. **RBAC authorizer** is purely additive and returns `NoOpinion` on miss. It reads from the informer cache; it cannot be influenced by runtime inputs other than changes to RBAC objects in etcd.\n4. **Webhook authorizer** receives the full `SubjectAccessReview` request. It is an external trust boundary \u2014 its security posture is entirely determined by the external service. It can return `Allow`, `Deny`, or `NoOpinion`. CEL match conditions (`Webhook.MatchConditions`) can be used to limit which requests are forwarded.\n\n### How the Authorizer Chain Interacts\n\n```\nRequest\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\n[system:masters group check]  \u2500\u2500\u2500 Allow \u2192 \u2713 (bypass all RBAC)\n  \u2502 NoOpinion\n  \u25bc\n[Node authorizer]             \u2500\u2500\u2500 Allow/Deny/NoOpinion\n  \u2502 NoOpinion\n  \u25bc\n[RBAC authorizer]             \u2500\u2500\u2500 Allow \u2192 \u2713 (with audit reason)\n  \u2502 NoOpinion (never Deny)\n  \u25bc\n[Webhook authorizer]          \u2500\u2500\u2500 Allow/Deny/NoOpinion\n  \u2502 NoOpinion (chain exhausted)\n  \u25bc\n[Implicit Deny] \u2192 403 Forbidden\n```\n\nErrors from individual authorizers are accumulated by the union but do not stop chain evaluation. The final aggregate error is only returned if no `Allow` or `Deny` was reached.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization subsystem is architecturally sound with a well-layered defense-in-depth design. The overall security posture is **strong** for correctly configured clusters, with the following key findings:\n\n**Strengths:**\n- Deny-by-default semantics: RBAC only allows, never explicitly denies, and the exhausted chain returns `403`.\n- Strict separation of authentication from authorization through the context pipeline.\n- `ConfirmNoEscalation` prevents RBAC objects from being used to self-grant permissions the grantor does not already hold.\n- Comprehensive audit trail: every authorization decision (allow, forbid, error) is annotated in the audit event with the decision and reason.\n- Policy data is isolated from request data: RBAC reads from the in-memory informer cache backed by etcd, preventing untrusted input from directly manipulating policy.\n- Authentication headers are aggressively stripped after authentication to prevent header injection attacks.\n\n**Key Security Risks:**\n1. **`system:masters` is an immutable superuser bypass** \u2014 not auditable via RBAC, must be controlled at the certificate/identity level.\n2. **RBAC never explicitly denies** \u2014 placement of `AlwaysAllow` after RBAC in the chain neutralizes all RBAC denials.\n3. **Impersonation is a privilege escalation vector** \u2014 RBAC rules granting `impersonate` on `groups` without restriction can allow escalation to `system:masters`.\n4. **Incomplete rule resolution is non-fatal** \u2014 errors in fetching roles are collected but evaluation continues; an intermittent informer outage could cause `ConfirmNoEscalation` to under-count the grantor's permissions.\n5. **Webhook `failurePolicy: NoOpinion`** means webhook unavailability silently falls through to RBAC-only authorization \u2014 operators may not notice the webhook is down.\n6. **The `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate** introduces field/label selector data from the request into the `AttributesRecord`, extending the untrusted input surface passed to webhook authorizers.\n\n**Recommendations:**\n- Audit all grants of `impersonate` permissions, especially for groups.\n- Never place `AlwaysAllow` in production authorization chains.\n- Configure webhook `failurePolicy: Deny` if the webhook is security-critical, or implement monitoring for webhook failures if `NoOpinion` is used.\n- Monitor audit events for `authorization.k8s.io/decision=allow` with reason strings indicating `system:masters` bypass.\n- Restrict access to `ClusterRole`, `ClusterRoleBinding`, `Role`, and `RoleBinding` write operations to a small set of administrative principals.\n",

  "security_risk": "LOW"
}

audit annotations `authorization.k8s.io/decision` and `authorization.k8s.io/reason` are set on every outcome\n\n### Critical Security Properties\n- **`system:masters` always bypasses RBAC** \u2014 `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` is unconditionally prepended to the chain in `reload.go`\n- **RBAC never explicitly denies** \u2014 placing `AlwaysAllow` after RBAC neutralizes all RBAC policies\n- **Impersonation is a high-privilege operation** \u2014 unrestricted `impersonate` grants on `groups` can escalate to `system:masters`\n- **Incomplete rule resolution is non-fatal** \u2014 informer cache errors during `ConfirmNoEscalation` checks may under-count grantor permissions\n- **Webhook `failurePolicy: NoOpinion`** silently falls through to RBAC-only if the webhook goes down\n- **`AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate** passes field/label selector query parameters through to webhook authorizers, extending the untrusted input surface"
